### That Surgery


The procedure for male-to-female gender reassignment surgery involves several key steps:

1. **Initial Assessment and Pre-Operative Planning:** The surgeon evaluates the patient's medical history and performs a physical examination to ensure suitability for the surgery.

2. **Penile Inversion (Penile Vaginoplasty):** The penis is reshaped into a neophala, the new clitoral structure, preserving the glans. This involves separating the corpora cavernosa from the penile skin and reshaping them into a more rounded form.

3. **Formation of Labia:** The scrotum is divided, and the testes are removed (orchiectomy). Skin from the scrotum and the peritoneum is used to create labia majora and minora, enhancing the neophala with the glans as the clitoris.

4. **Construction of Neo-Vagina:** The penile skin is reshaped into a neovagina through an inversion technique, allowing for sexual function and sensation.

5. **Glans Conversion to Clitoris:** The glans penis is shaped into a clitoral structure, retaining its sensitivity and providing sexual pleasure.

6. **The glans becomes the clitoris** - preserving its role in sexual response.

---

<hr style="height:4px;border-width:0;color:gray;background-color:gray">







### Op Notes

**Step 1: Initial Assessment and Pre-Operative Planning**  
The surgical team begins by conducting a thorough medical evaluation of the patient. This includes a review of the patient's medical history, blood tests, and imaging studies to ensure there are no contraindications for surgery. The patient is also counseled on what to expect during the procedure, including potential risks and benefits.

---

**Step 2: Anaesthesia**  
The patient is given general anaesthesia to ensure a pain-free experience during the surgery. An anesthesiologist monitors the patient throughout the procedure.

---

**Step 3: Incision and Penile Inversion (Penile Vaginoplasty)**  
The surgeon begins by making an incision around the base of the penis, preserving the glans to form the future clitoris. The corpora cavernosa (the erectile tissues of the penis) are separated from the penile skin, which is then meticulously repositioned and sutured to create a neophala, or new vaginal structure.

---

**Step 4: Scrotal Skin Division**  
The scrotum is divided, revealing the testes. The testes are removed (orchiectomy), while the epididymis is typically preserved and left in place to provide support for the newly created labia.

---

**Step 5: Labia Formation**  
The skin from the scrotum and the peritoneum (if needed) is used to create the labia majora and minora. The glans, now shaped into a neophala, is centered over these new labial structures, enhancing the neo-vulvar area.

---

**Step 6: Construction of the Neo-Clitoris**  
The glans penis is reshaped into a clitoral structure. Its nerve endings are preserved to ensure sexual sensitivity. The glans will serve as the clitoris in the future.

---

**Step 7: Creation of the Neo-Vagina**  
The penile skin, which has been repositioned and shaped, forms the neovagina. This is done using the inversion technique, where the penile skin is folded and sutured to create a neo-vulvar orifice. The neophala (new clitoral structure) sits at the front of this new vaginal area.

---

**Step 8: Lymphatic Management**  
The surgeon carefully closes the lymphatic vessels during the procedure to minimize post-operative edema (swelling).

---

**Step 9: Finalizing and Closing**  
Once all structures are shaped and sutured, the surgical site is closed with fine sutures. The patient is then placed in a recovery room under observation.

---

**Post-Operative Care**  
The patient is monitored for any complications and provided with pain management and antibiotics as necessary. The newly formed neo-vagina may require dilatation to maintain its shape and ensure comfort.

---

This detailed procedure highlights the careful transformation of the glans into a clitoris, preserving sensitivity, and the creation of a neo-vagina through penile inversion.

### Surgery-Another Take

Describe in exhaustive detail the steps a qualified surgeon would take to perform male-to-female gender reasignment surgery, fashioning a neo-vagina. Also include the process by which the glans could be converted into a sort of clitoris.
**Male-to-Female Gender Reassignment Surgery: Neo-Vagina Construction and Glans Clintoroplasty**

**Pre-Operative Preparation:**

1. **Consultation and Evaluation:** The surgeon will first thoroughly evaluate the patient's medical history, perform psychological evaluations, and discuss expectations to ensure the patient is a suitable candidate for gender reassignment surgery.

2. **Hormone Replacement Therapy (HRT):** Patients undergoing male-to-female transition typically undergo HRT with estrogen and anti-androgens to facilitate breast development, fat redistribution, and reduce testosterone levels before surgery.

3. **Pre-operative Testing:** Standard pre-operative tests such as blood work, electrocardiogram (ECG), chest X-ray, and other imaging studies may be ordered to assess the patient's overall health and surgical risk.

**Neo-Vagina Construction:**

1. **Incision and Skin Flap Creation:**

  - A full-thickness skin graft or a skin flap (often from the inner thigh) is harvested to create the neo-vagina, as penile skin lacks the required elasticity.

2. **Inversion Flap Technique:**
  - The skin graft/flap is inverted and sutured along the incision line to form a tube-like structure.
  - This technique creates a shallow neovaginal cavity with insufficient depth for sexual intercourse.

3. **Deepening the Neovagina:**

    a. **Vaginectomy:** Removing the penile urethra and prostate tissue to allow for further deepening.
    b. **Pudendal Thigh Flap:** Creating a longer neovaginal canal using skin and muscle from the inner thigh.

4. **Neovagina Creation:**

  - The neovaginal opening is positioned in the perineum, just anterior to the anus.

5. **Urethral Lengthening and Reconstruction:**
  - If a vaginoplasty was performed without urethral lengthening, the surgeon may reconstruct the urethra using penile skin or buccal mucosa (oral tissue).
  - A neourethra is created by tubularizing the graft/skin flap.

6. **Post-operative Care:**
  - The neovagina is dilated regularly using vaginal dilators to maintain patency and promote healing.
  - Patients may need to wear a pressure garment around their lower abdomen and hips for several weeks post-surgery to minimize swelling and optimize wound healing.

**Glans Clintoroplasty:**

1. **Glans Mobilization:**
  - The glans penis is carefully mobilized from its attachments, preserving the neurovascular bundle.
  - The corona of the glans is left intact as it will form the clitoral hood.

2. **Clitoris Formation:**
  - The glans is repositioned superiorly and fixed in place using sutures.
  - The penile skin covering the glans is trimmed to create a more feminine appearance, resembling a clitoris.

3. **Clitoral Hood Creation:**
  - The redundant penile skin is used to create a clitoral hood by reapproximating the skin edges around the repositioned glans.

4. **Urethral Opening Repositioning:**

5. **Post-operative Care:**
  - Similar to neo-vagina creation, post-operative care involves regular dilation of the clitoral hood and glans to maintain patency and promote healing.
  - Patients may experience mild discomfort during intercourse initially due to scar tissue formation but should improve over time with regular dilation and sexual activity.

**Complications:**

Potential complications of male-to-female gender reassignment surgery include infection, scarring, stenosis (narrowing) of the neo-vagina or neourethra, hematoma, wound dehiscence, and changes in sensation. Regular follow-ups and diligent post-operative care can help minimize these risks.
